Marx viewed [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") as the main counter-revolutionary threat to European revolutions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649–239_254-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649%E2%80%93239-254">[253]</a></sup> During the [Crimean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_War "Crimean War"), Marx backed the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") and its allies Britain and France against Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649–239_254-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649%E2%80%93239-254">[253]</a></sup> He was absolutely opposed to [Pan-Slavism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Slavism "Pan-Slavism"), viewing it as an instrument of Russian foreign policy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649–239_254-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649%E2%80%93239-254">[253]</a></sup> Marx had considered the [Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavs "Slavs") nations except [Poles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_people "Polish people") as 'counter-revolutionary'. Marx and Engels published in the _[Neue Rheinische Zeitung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neue_Rheinische_Zeitung "Neue Rheinische Zeitung")_ in February 1849:

> To the sentimental phrases about brotherhood which we are being offered here on behalf of the most counter-revolutionary nations of Europe, we reply that hatred of Russians was and still is the primary revolutionary passion among Germans; that since the [revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848 "Revolutions of 1848") \[of 1848\] hatred of Czechs and Croats has been added, and that only by the most determined use of terror against these Slav peoples can we, jointly with the Poles and Magyars, safeguard the revolution. We know where the enemies of the revolution are concentrated, _viz_. in Russia and the Slav regions of Austria, and no fine phrases, no allusions to an undefined democratic future for these countries can deter us from treating our enemies as enemies. Then there will be a struggle, an "inexorable life-and-death struggle", against those Slavs who betray the revolution; an annihilating fight and ruthless terror – not in the interests of Germany, but in the interests of the revolution!"<sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-255">[254]</a></sup>

Marx and Engels sympathised with the [Narodnik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narodniks "Narodniks") revolutionaries of the 1860s and 1870s. When the [Russian revolutionaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narodnaya_Volya "Narodnaya Volya") assassinated Tsar [Alexander II of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia "Alexander II of Russia"), Marx expressed the hope that the assassination foreshadowed 'the formation of a Russian commune'.<sup id="cite_ref-256"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-256">[255]</a></sup> Marx supported the [Polish uprisings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Russian_Wars "Polish–Russian Wars") against tsarist Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649–239_254-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson201649%E2%80%93239-254">[253]</a></sup> He said in a speech in London in 1867:

> In the first place the policy of Russia is changeless... Its methods, its tactics, its manoeuvres may change, but the polar star of its policy – world domination – is a fixed star. In our times only a civilised government ruling over barbarian masses can hatch out such a plan and execute it. ... There is but one alternative for Europe. Either Asiatic barbarism, under Muscovite direction, will burst around its head like an avalanche, or else it must re-establish Poland, thus putting twenty million heroes between itself and Asia and gaining a breathing spell for the accomplishment of its social regeneration.<sup id="cite_ref-257"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-257">[256]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/India-7669_-_Flickr_-_archer10_%28Dennis%29.jpg/220px-India-7669_-_Flickr_-_archer10_%28Dennis%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:India-7669_-_Flickr_-_archer10_(Dennis).jpg)

[CPI(M)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_India_(Marxist) "Communist Party of India (Marxist)") poster in [Kerala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala "Kerala"), India

Marx supported the cause of [Irish independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule_movement "Irish Home Rule movement"). In 1867, he wrote Engels: "I used to think the separation of Ireland from England impossible. I now think it inevitable. The English working class will never accomplish anything until it has got rid of Ireland. ... English reaction in England had its roots ... in the subjugation of Ireland."<sup id="cite_ref-258"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-258">[257]</a></sup>

Marx spent some time in [French Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Algeria "French Algeria"), which had been [invaded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_conquest_of_Algeria "French conquest of Algeria") and made a [French colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_colonial_empire "French colonial empire") in 1830, and had the opportunity to observe life in colonial North Africa. He wrote about the colonial justice system, in which "a form of torture has been used (and this happens 'regularly') to extract confessions from the Arabs; naturally it is done (like the English in India) by the 'police'; the judge is supposed to know nothing at all about it."<sup id="cite_ref-alahram_259-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-alahram-259">[258]</a></sup> Marx was surprised by the arrogance of many [European settlers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pied-Noir "Pied-Noir") in Algiers and wrote in a letter: "when a European colonist dwells among the 'lesser breeds,' either as a settler or even on business, he generally regards himself as even more inviolable than handsome William I \[a Prussian king\]. Still, when it comes to bare-faced arrogance and presumptuousness vis-à-vis the 'lesser breeds,' the British and Dutch outdo the French."<sup id="cite_ref-alahram_259-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-alahram-259">[258]</a></sup>

According to the _[Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_Encyclopedia_of_Philosophy "Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy")_: "Marx's analysis of colonialism as a progressive force bringing modernization to a backward feudal society sounds like a transparent rationalization for foreign domination. His account of British domination, however, reflects the same ambivalence that he shows towards capitalism in Europe. In both cases, Marx recognizes the immense suffering brought about during the transition from feudal to bourgeois society while insisting that the transition is both necessary and ultimately progressive. He argues that the penetration of foreign commerce will cause a social revolution in India."<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-260">[259]</a></sup>

Marx discussed [British](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") [colonial rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Raj "British Raj") in [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_India "Colonial India") in the _[New York Herald Tribune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Herald_Tribune "New York Herald Tribune")_ in June 1853:

> There cannot remain any doubt but that the misery inflicted by the British on Hindostan \[India\] is of an essentially different and infinitely more intensive kind than all Hindostan had to suffer before. England has broken down the entire framework of Indian society, without any symptoms of reconstitution yet appearing... \[however\], we must not forget that these idyllic village communities, inoffensive though they may appear, had always been the solid foundation of Oriental despotism, that they restrained the human mind within the smallest possible compass, making it the unresisting tool of superstition.<sup id="cite_ref-alahram_259-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-alahram-259">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-261">[260]</a></sup>

## Legacy

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Marx_und_Engels_Denkmal%2C_alter_Platz_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Marx_und_Engels_Denkmal%2C_alter_Platz_-_panoramio.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Marx_und_Engels_Denkmal,_alter_Platz_-_panoramio.jpg)

Karl Marx and Friedrich Engels monument in [Marx-Engels Forum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marx-Engels_Forum "Marx-Engels Forum"), [Berlin-Mitte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin-Mitte "Berlin-Mitte"), Germany

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Stamp_Soviet_Union_1948_CPA_1246.jpg/220px-Stamp_Soviet_Union_1948_CPA_1246.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Stamp_Soviet_Union_1948_CPA_1246.jpg)

1948 [Soviet Union stamp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union_stamp_catalogue "Soviet Union stamp catalogue"), featuring Marx and Engels, commemorating the 100th anniversary of the _Manifesto_

Marx's ideas have had a profound impact on world politics and intellectual thought,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun200223–24_7-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun200223%E2%80%9324-7">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Manchester_8-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-Manchester-8">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-262">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Allan2010_263-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-Allan2010-263">[262]</a></sup> in particular in the aftermath of the 1917 Russian Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-264"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-264">[263]</a></sup> Followers of Marx have often debated among themselves over how to interpret Marx's writings and apply his concepts to the modern world.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAndersenKaspersen2000123–_265-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAndersenKaspersen2000123%E2%80%93-265">[264]</a></sup> The legacy of Marx's thought has become contested between numerous tendencies, each of which sees itself as Marx's most accurate interpreter. In the political realm, these tendencies include [political theories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_theories "Political theories") such as [Leninism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leninism "Leninism"), [Marxism–Leninism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism "Marxism–Leninism"), [Trotskyism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trotskyism "Trotskyism"), [Maoism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maoism "Maoism"), [Luxemburgism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxemburgism "Luxemburgism"), [libertarian Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libertarian_Marxism "Libertarian Marxism"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAndersenKaspersen2000123–_265-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAndersenKaspersen2000123%E2%80%93-265">[264]</a></sup> and [Open Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_Marxism "Open Marxism"). Various currents have also developed in [academic Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_Marxism "Academic Marxism"), often under influence of other views, resulting in [structuralist Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Structuralist_Marxism "Structuralist Marxism"), [historical materialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_materialism "Historical materialism"), phenomenological Marxism, [analytical Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytical_Marxism "Analytical Marxism"), and [Hegelian Marxism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hegelian_Marxism "Hegelian Marxism").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAndersenKaspersen2000123–_265-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAndersenKaspersen2000123%E2%80%93-265">[264]</a></sup>

From an academic perspective, Marx's work contributed to the birth of modern sociology. He has been cited as one of the 19th century's three masters of the "[school of suspicion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermeneutics_of_suspicion "Hermeneutics of suspicion")", alongside [Friedrich Nietzsche](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche "Friedrich Nietzsche") and [Sigmund Freud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sigmund_Freud "Sigmund Freud"),<sup id="cite_ref-266"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-266">[265]</a></sup> and as one of the three principal architects of modern [social science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_science "Social science") along with [Émile Durkheim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89mile_Durkheim "Émile Durkheim") and [Max Weber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Max_Weber "Max Weber").<sup id="cite_ref-plato.stanford.edu_267-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-plato.stanford.edu-267">[266]</a></sup> In contrast to other philosophers, Marx offered theories that could often be tested with the [scientific method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_method "Scientific method").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun200223–24_7-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun200223%E2%80%9324-7">[6]</a></sup> Both Marx and [Auguste Comte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auguste_Comte "Auguste Comte") set out to develop scientifically justified ideologies in the wake of European [secularisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secularisation "Secularisation") and new developments in the [philosophies of history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy_of_history "Philosophy of history") and science. Working in the Hegelian tradition, Marx rejected Comtean [sociological positivism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociological_positivism "Sociological positivism") in an attempt to develop a _science of society_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalhoun200219_268-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalhoun200219-268">[267]</a></sup> [Karl Löwith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_L%C3%B6with "Karl Löwith") considered Marx and [Søren Kierkegaard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%B8ren_Kierkegaard "Søren Kierkegaard") to be the two greatest philosophical successors of Hegel.<sup id="cite_ref-269"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-269">[268]</a></sup> In modern [sociological theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociological_theory "Sociological theory"), [Marxist sociology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist_sociology "Marxist sociology") is recognised as one of the main classical perspectives. [Isaiah Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_Berlin "Isaiah Berlin") considers Marx the true founder of modern sociology "in so far as anyone can claim the title".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBerlin1963130_270-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBerlin1963130-270">[269]</a></sup> Beyond social science, he has also had a lasting legacy in philosophy, literature, the arts, and the humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESinger19801_271-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTESinger19801-271">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-272">[271]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-273">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-274">[273]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Karl-Marx-Statue_in_Trier.jpg/170px-Karl-Marx-Statue_in_Trier.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Karl-Marx-Statue_in_Trier.jpg)

Marx statue in Trier, Germany

Social theorists of the 20th and 21st centuries have pursued two main strategies in response to Marx. One move has been to reduce it to its analytical core, known as analytical Marxism. Another, more common move has been to dilute the explanatory claims of Marx's social theory and emphasise the "relative autonomy" of aspects of social and economic life not directly related to Marx's central narrative of interaction between the development of the "forces of production" and the succession of "modes of production". This has been the [neo-Marxist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Marxist "Neo-Marxist") theorising adopted by historians inspired by Marx's social theory such as [E. P. Thompson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E._P._Thompson "E. P. Thompson") and Eric Hobsbawm. It has also been a line of thinking pursued by thinkers and activists such as [Antonio Gramsci](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonio_Gramsci "Antonio Gramsci") who have sought to understand the opportunities and the difficulties of transformative political practice, seen in the light of Marxist social theory.<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-275">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-276">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-277">[276]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-278">[277]</a></sup> Marx's ideas would also have a profound influence on subsequent artists and art history, with avant-garde movements across literature, visual art, music, film, and theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-279"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-279">[278]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Communist_countries.svg/300px-Communist_countries.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Communist_countries.svg)

Map of countries that declared themselves to be socialist states under the [Marxist–Leninist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism "Marxism–Leninism") or [Maoist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maoism "Maoism") definition between 1979 and 1983, which marked the greatest territorial extent of [socialist states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_socialist_states "List of socialist states")

Politically, Marx's legacy is more complex. Throughout the 20th century, revolutions in dozens of countries labelled themselves "Marxist"—most notably the [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution"), which led to the founding of the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union").<sup id="cite_ref-April_Thesis_280-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-April_Thesis-280">[279]</a></sup> Major world leaders including [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin"),<sup id="cite_ref-April_Thesis_280-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-April_Thesis-280">[279]</a></sup> [Mao Zedong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong"),<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-281">[280]</a></sup> [Fidel Castro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fidel_Castro "Fidel Castro"),<sup id="cite_ref-282"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-282">[281]</a></sup> [Salvador Allende](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salvador_Allende "Salvador Allende"),<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-283">[282]</a></sup> [Josip Broz Tito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito "Josip Broz Tito"),<sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-284">[283]</a></sup> [Kwame Nkrumah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah "Kwame Nkrumah"),<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-285">[284]</a></sup> [Jawaharlal Nehru](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru "Jawaharlal Nehru"),<sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-286">[285]</a></sup> [Nelson Mandela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelson_Mandela "Nelson Mandela"),<sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-287">[286]</a></sup> [Xi Jinping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xi_Jinping "Xi Jinping")<sup id="cite_ref-euronews_288-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-euronews-288">[287]</a></sup> and [Thomas Sankara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Sankara "Thomas Sankara")<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-289">[288]</a></sup> have all cited Marx as an influence. Beyond where Marxist revolutions took place, Marx's ideas have informed political parties worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-290"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-290">[289]</a></sup> In countries associated with Marxism, some events have led political opponents to blame Marx for millions of deaths,<sup id="cite_ref-291"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-291">[290]</a></sup> while others argue for a distinction between the legacy and influence of Marx specifically, and the legacy and influence of those who have shaped his ideas for political purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-292">[291]</a></sup> Arthur Lipow describes Marx and his collaborator [Friedrich Engels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Engels "Friedrich Engels") as "the founders of modern revolutionary democratic socialism."<sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-293">[292]</a></sup>

The cities of [Marks, Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marks,_Russia "Marks, Russia") and [Karl-Marx-Stadt, Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemnitz "Chemnitz") (now known as Chemnitz) were named after Marx.<sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-294">[293]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-295">[294]</a></sup> In May 2018, to mark the bicentenary of his birth, a 4.5m statue of him by leading Chinese sculptor [Wu Weishan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wu_Weishan "Wu Weishan") and donated by the Chinese government was unveiled in his birthplace of [Trier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trier "Trier"), Germany. The then-[European Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission") president [Jean-Claude Juncker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker "Jean-Claude Juncker") defended Marx's memory, saying that today Marx "stands for things which he is not responsible for and which he didn't cause because many of the things he wrote down were redrafted into the opposite".<sup id="cite_ref-independent_296-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-independent-296">[295]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-297">[296]</a></sup>

In 2017, a feature film, titled _[The Young Karl Marx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Young_Karl_Marx "The Young Karl Marx")_, featuring Marx, his wife [Jenny Marx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jenny_Marx "Jenny Marx"), and Engels, among other revolutionaries and intellectuals prior to the [Revolutions of 1848](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848 "Revolutions of 1848"), received good reviews for both its historical accuracy and its brio in dealing with intellectual life.<sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-298">[297]</a></sup>

## Selected bibliography

-   _[The Difference Between the Democritean and Epicurean Philosophy of Nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Difference_Between_the_Democritean_and_Epicurean_Philosophy_of_Nature "The Difference Between the Democritean and Epicurean Philosophy of Nature")_ (doctoral thesis),<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-299">[298]</a></sup> 1841

-   [Notes on James Mill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Notes_on_James_Mill "Notes on James Mill"), 1844
-   _[Economic and Philosophic Manuscripts of 1844](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_and_Philosophic_Manuscripts_of_1844 "Economic and Philosophic Manuscripts of 1844")_, 1844
-   _[The Holy Family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holy_Family_(book) "The Holy Family (book)")_, 1845
-   [Theses on Feuerbach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theses_on_Feuerbach "Theses on Feuerbach"), written 1845, first published posthumously 1888 by Engels.
-   _[The German Ideology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_German_Ideology "The German Ideology")_, 1845
-   _[The Poverty of Philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Poverty_of_Philosophy "The Poverty of Philosophy")_, 1847
-   [Wage Labour and Capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wage_Labour_and_Capital "Wage Labour and Capital"), 1847

-   _[The Class Struggles in France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Class_Struggles_in_France_1848-1850 "The Class Struggles in France 1848-1850")_, 1850
-   _[The Eighteenth Brumaire of Louis Napoleon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Eighteenth_Brumaire_of_Louis_Napoleon "The Eighteenth Brumaire of Louis Napoleon")_, 1852
-   _[Grundrisse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grundrisse "Grundrisse") (Foundations of a Critique of Political Economy)_, 1857

-   _[Theories of Surplus Value](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theories_of_Surplus_Value "Theories of Surplus Value")_, (posthumously published by [Kautsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Kautsky "Karl Kautsky")) 3 volumes, 1862
-   _[Address of the International Working Men's Association to Abraham Lincoln](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Address_of_the_International_Working_Men%27s_Association_to_Abraham_Lincoln "Address of the International Working Men's Association to Abraham Lincoln")_, 1864
-   [Value, Price and Profit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value,_Price_and_Profit "Value, Price and Profit"), 1865
-   _[Capital. Volume I: A Critique of Political Economy The Process of Production of Capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital,_Volume_I "Capital, Volume I")_ (_Das Kapital_), 1867
-   [The Civil War in France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Civil_War_in_France "The Civil War in France"), 1871
-   [Critique of the Gotha Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critique_of_the_Gotha_Program "Critique of the Gotha Program"), 1875
-   [Notes on Adolph Wagner](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Notes_on_Adolph_Wagner&action=edit&redlink=1 "Notes on Adolph Wagner (page does not exist)"), 1883
-   [_Das Kapital_, Volume II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital,_Volume_II "Capital, Volume II") (posthumously published by Engels), 1885
-   [_Das Kapital_, Volume III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital,_Volume_III "Capital, Volume III") (posthumously published by Engels), 1894

## Notes

1.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_ref-3 "Jump up")** His name was spelled _Carl Marx_ in the birth register of [Trier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trier "Trier") and he occasionally used this spelling in official contexts up to the 1840s. His full name is sometimes given as _Karl Heinrich Marx_, but he never officially had a middle name, using the forms _Karl Heinrich_ or _Carl Heinrich_ (with his father's first name added after his own) only several times as a student.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinrich201934–35_2-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinrich201934%E2%80%9335-2">[2]</a></sup>

[Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20190318101547/https://plato.stanford.edu/archives/win2017/entries/weber/) from the original on 18 March 2019. Retrieved 10 December 2017. Max Weber is known as a principal architect of modern social science along with Karl Marx and Emil Durkheim.

167.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPostone199354%E2%80%9355,_173,_192_168-0 "Jump up")** [Postone 1993](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#CITEREFPostone1993), pp. 54–55, 173, 192.
168.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_ref-169 "Jump up")** Marx. ["Economic Manuscripts: Appendix I: Production, Consumption, Distribution, Exchange"](https://www.marxists.org/archive/marx/works/1859/critique-pol-economy/appx1.htm#205). _www.marxists.org_. Retrieved 28 March 2022. \[...\] The solitary and isolated hunter or fisherman, who serves Adam Smith and Ricardo as a starting point, is one of the unimaginative fantasies of eighteenth-century romances a la Robinson Crusoe; and despite the assertions of social historians, these by no means signify simply a reaction against over-refinement and reversion to a misconceived natural life. \[...\] This is an illusion and nothing but the aesthetic illusion of the small and big Robinsonades. It is, on the contrary, the anticipation of "bourgeois society," which began to evolve in the sixteenth century and in the eighteenth century made giant strides towards maturity. The individual in this society of free competition seems to be rid of natural ties, etc., which made him an appurtenance of a particular, limited aggregation of human beings in previous historical epochs. The prophets of the eighteenth century, on whose shoulders Adam Smith and Ricardo were still wholly standing, envisaged this 18th-century individual – a product of the dissolution of feudal society on the one hand and of the new productive forces evolved since the sixteenth century on the other – as an ideal whose existence belonged to the past. They saw this individual not as an historical result, but as the starting point of history  
    \[...\]  
    Labour seems to be a very simple category. The notion of labour in this universal form, as labour in general, is also extremely old. Nevertheless "labour" in this simplicity is economically considered just as modern a category as the relations which give rise to this simple abstraction.
169.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_ref-:0_170-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_ref-:0_170-1) [_Classical sociological theory_](https://www.worldcat.org/oclc/794037359). Craig J. Calhoun (3rd ed.). Chichester, West Sussex: [John Wiley & Sons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Wiley_%26_Sons "John Wiley & Sons"). 2012. p. 138. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-0-470-65567-2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-470-65567-2 "Special:BookSources/978-0-470-65567-2"). [OCLC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC_(identifier) "OCLC (identifier)") [794037359](https://www.worldcat.org/oclc/794037359). Marx used social criticism as his standard form of social analysis. Marx defined criticism as the "radical negation of social reality."

188.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_ref-189 "Jump up")** [Lafargue, Paul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Lafargue "Paul Lafargue") (1972). [Marx–Engels–Lenin Institute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marx%E2%80%93Engels%E2%80%93Lenin_Institute "Marx–Engels–Lenin Institute") (ed.). [Reminiscences of Marx _(September 1890)_](https://www.marxists.org/archive/lafargue/1890/xx/marx.htm). Progress Publishers. He was a loving, gentle and indulgent father. \[...\] There was never even a trace of the bossy parent in his relations with his daughters, whose love for him was extraordinary. He never gave them an order, but asked them to do what he wished as a favour or made them feel that they should not do what he wanted to forbid them. And yet a father could seldom have had more docile children than he.

["Critique of the Gotha Programme, Part IV"](https://www.marxists.org/archive/marx/works/1875/gotha/ch04.htm). _Marx/Engels Selected Works_. Vol. 3. Moscow: Progress Publishers. pp. 13–30. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20190702071606/https://www.marxists.org/archive/marx/works/1875/gotha/ch04.htm) from the original on 2 July 2019 – via marxists.org.
251.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx#cite_ref-253 "Jump up")** [La Liberté Speech](https://www.marxists.org/archive/marx/works/1872/09/08.htm) [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20180716015355/https://www.marxists.org/archive/marx/works/1872/09/08.htm) 16 July 2018 at the [Wayback Machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayback_Machine "Wayback Machine") delivered by Karl Marx on 8 September 1872, in [Amsterdam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amsterdam "Amsterdam"). "You know that the institutions, mores, and traditions of various countries must be taken into consideration, and we do not deny that there are countries – such as America, England, and if I were more familiar with your institutions, I would perhaps also add Holland – where the workers can attain their goal by peaceful means. This being the case, we must also recognise the fact that in most countries on the Continent the lever of our revolution must be force; it is force to which we must some day appeal to erect the rule of labour."

[University of California Press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California_Press "University of California Press"). p. 1. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-0-520-07543-6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-520-07543-6 "Special:BookSources/978-0-520-07543-6"). 'We are not among those communists who are out to destroy personal liberty, who wish to turn the world into one huge barrack or into a gigantic workhouse. There certainly are some communists who, with an easy conscience, refuse to countenance personal liberty and would like to shuffle it out of the world because they consider that it is a hindrance to complete harmony. But we have no desire to exchange freedom for equality. We are convinced ... that in no social order will freedom be assured as in a society based upon communal ownership.' Thus wrote the editors of the _Journal_ of the Communist League in 1847, under the direct influence of the founders of modern revolutionary democratic socialism, Karl Marx and Frederick Engels.

(ed.), _Kalecki's Relevance Today_, London, Macmillan, [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-0-312-02411-6](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-312-02411-6 "Special:BookSources/978-0-312-02411-6").
